Rexroth\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_author_institution\" content=\"Laboratoire d\u2019Astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne, Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290 Versoix, Switzerland\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_title\" content=\"Strong-lensing analysis of MACS\u2009J0717.5+3745 from Hubble Frontier Fields observations: How well can the mass distribution be constrained?\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_online_date\" content=\"2016/03/24\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_publication_date\" content=\"2016/04/01\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_volume\" content=\"588\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_firstpage\" content=\"A99\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_doi\" content=\"10.1051/0004-6361/201527638\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_bibcode\" content=\"2016A%26A...588A..99L\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/abs/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_fulltext_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/full_html/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_pdf_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/pdf/2016/04/aa27638-15.pdf\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"0004-6361\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"1432-0746\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_language\" content=\"en\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: strong\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: clusters: individual: MACS J0717.5+3745\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"We present a strong-lensing analysis of MACSJ0717.5+3745 (hereafter MACS\u2009J0717), based on the full depth of the &lt;i&gt;Hubble &lt;i/&gt;Frontier Field (HFF) observations, which brings the number of multiply imaged systems to 61, ten of which have been spectroscopically confirmed. The total number of images comprised in these systems rises to 165, compared to 48 images in 16 systems before the HFF observations. Our analysis uses a parametric mass reconstruction technique, as implemented in the Lenstool software, and the subset of the 132 most secure multiple images to constrain a mass distribution composed of four large-scale mass components (spatially aligned with the four main light concentrations) and a multitude of galaxy-scale perturbers. We find a superposition of cored isothermal mass components to provide a good fit to the observational constraints, resulting in a very shallow mass distribution for the smooth (large-scale) component. Given the implications of such a flat mass profile, we investigate whether a model composed of \u201cpeaky\u201d non-cored mass components can also reproduce the observational constraints. We find that such a non-cored mass model reproduces the observational constraints equally well, in the sense that both models give comparable total rms. Although the total (smooth dark matter component plus galaxy-scale perturbers) mass distributions of both models are consistent, as are the integrated two-dimensional mass profiles, we find that the smooth and the galaxy-scale components are very different. We conclude that, even in the HFF era, the generic degeneracy between smooth and galaxy-scale components is not broken, in particular in such a complex galaxy cluster. Consequently, insights into the mass distribution of MACS\u2009J0717 remain limited, emphasizing the need for additional probes beyond strong lensing. Our findings also have implications for estimates of the lensing magnification. We show that the amplification difference between the two models is larger than the error associated with either model, and that this additional systematic uncertainty is approximately the difference in magnification obtained by the different groups of modelers using pre-HFF data. This uncertainty decreases the area of the image plane where we can reliably study the high-redshift Universe by 50 to 70%.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A. Rexroth\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_author_institution\" content=\"Laboratoire d\u2019Astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne, Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290 Versoix, Switzerland\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_title\" content=\"Strong-lensing analysis of MACS\u2009J0717.5+3745 from Hubble Frontier Fields observations: How well can the mass distribution be constrained?\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_online_date\" content=\"2016/03/24\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_publication_date\" content=\"2016/04/01\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_volume\" content=\"588\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_firstpage\" content=\"A99\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_doi\" content=\"10.1051/0004-6361/201527638\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_bibcode\" content=\"2016A%26A...588A..99L\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/abs/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_fulltext_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/full_html/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_pdf_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/pdf/2016/04/aa27638-15.pdf\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"0004-6361\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"1432-0746\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_language\" content=\"en\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: strong\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: clusters: individual: MACS J0717.5+3745\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"We present a strong-lensing analysis of MACSJ0717.5+3745 (hereafter MACS\u2009J0717), based on the full depth of the &lt;i&gt;Hubble &lt;i/&gt;Frontier Field (HFF) observations, which brings the number of multiply imaged systems to 61, ten of which have been spectroscopically confirmed. The total number of images comprised in these systems rises to 165, compared to 48 images in 16 systems before the HFF observations. Our analysis uses a parametric mass reconstruction technique, as implemented in the Lenstool software, and the subset of the 132 most secure multiple images to constrain a mass distribution composed of four large-scale mass components (spatially aligned with the four main light concentrations) and a multitude of galaxy-scale perturbers. We find a superposition of cored isothermal mass components to provide a good fit to the observational constraints, resulting in a very shallow mass distribution for the smooth (large-scale) component. Given the implications of such a flat mass profile, we investigate whether a model composed of \u201cpeaky\u201d non-cored mass components can also reproduce the observational constraints. We find that such a non-cored mass model reproduces the observational constraints equally well, in the sense that both models give comparable total rms. Although the total (smooth dark matter component plus galaxy-scale perturbers) mass distributions of both models are consistent, as are the integrated two-dimensional mass profiles, we find that the smooth and the galaxy-scale components are very different. We conclude that, even in the HFF era, the generic degeneracy between smooth and galaxy-scale components is not broken, in particular in such a complex galaxy cluster. Consequently, insights into the mass distribution of MACS\u2009J0717 remain limited, emphasizing the need for additional probes beyond strong lensing. Our findings also have implications for estimates of the lensing magnification. We show that the amplification difference between the two models is larger than the error associated with either model, and that this additional systematic uncertainty is approximately the difference in magnification obtained by the different groups of modelers using pre-HFF data. This uncertainty decreases the area of the image plane where we can reliably study the high-redshift Universe by 50 to 70%.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A. Rexroth\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_author_institution\" content=\"Laboratoire d\u2019Astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne, Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290 Versoix, Switzerland\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_title\" content=\"Strong-lensing analysis of MACS\u2009J0717.5+3745 from Hubble Frontier Fields observations: How well can the mass distribution be constrained?\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_online_date\" content=\"2016/03/24\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_publication_date\" content=\"2016/04/01\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_volume\" content=\"588\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_firstpage\" content=\"A99\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_doi\" content=\"10.1051/0004-6361/201527638\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_bibcode\" content=\"2016A%26A...588A..99L\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/abs/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_fulltext_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/full_html/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_pdf_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/pdf/2016/04/aa27638-15.pdf\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"0004-6361\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"1432-0746\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_language\" content=\"en\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: strong\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: clusters: individual: MACS J0717.5+3745\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"We present a strong-lensing analysis of MACSJ0717.5+3745 (hereafter MACS\u2009J0717), based on the full depth of the &lt;i&gt;Hubble &lt;i/&gt;Frontier Field (HFF) observations, which brings the number of multiply imaged systems to 61, ten of which have been spectroscopically confirmed. The total number of images comprised in these systems rises to 165, compared to 48 images in 16 systems before the HFF observations. Our analysis uses a parametric mass reconstruction technique, as implemented in the Lenstool software, and the subset of the 132 most secure multiple images to constrain a mass distribution composed of four large-scale mass components (spatially aligned with the four main light concentrations) and a multitude of galaxy-scale perturbers. We find a superposition of cored isothermal mass components to provide a good fit to the observational constraints, resulting in a very shallow mass distribution for the smooth (large-scale) component. Given the implications of such a flat mass profile, we investigate whether a model composed of \u201cpeaky\u201d non-cored mass components can also reproduce the observational constraints. We find that such a non-cored mass model reproduces the observational constraints equally well, in the sense that both models give comparable total rms. Although the total (smooth dark matter component plus galaxy-scale perturbers) mass distributions of both models are consistent, as are the integrated two-dimensional mass profiles, we find that the smooth and the galaxy-scale components are very different. We conclude that, even in the HFF era, the generic degeneracy between smooth and galaxy-scale components is not broken, in particular in such a complex galaxy cluster. Consequently, insights into the mass distribution of MACS\u2009J0717 remain limited, emphasizing the need for additional probes beyond strong lensing. Our findings also have implications for estimates of the lensing magnification. We show that the amplification difference between the two models is larger than the error associated with either model, and that this additional systematic uncertainty is approximately the difference in magnification obtained by the different groups of modelers using pre-HFF data. This uncertainty decreases the area of the image plane where we can reliably study the high-redshift Universe by 50 to 70%.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A. Rexroth\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_author_institution\" content=\"Laboratoire d\u2019Astrophysique, \u00c9cole Polytechnique F\u00e9d\u00e9rale de Lausanne, Observatoire de Sauverny, 1290 Versoix, Switzerland\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_title\" content=\"Strong-lensing analysis of MACS\u2009J0717.5+3745 from Hubble Frontier Fields observations: How well can the mass distribution be constrained?\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_online_date\" content=\"2016/03/24\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_publication_date\" content=\"2016/04/01\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_volume\" content=\"588\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_firstpage\" content=\"A99\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_doi\" content=\"10.1051/0004-6361/201527638\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_bibcode\" content=\"2016A%26A...588A..99L\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/abs/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_fulltext_html_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/full_html/2016/04/aa27638-15/aa27638-15.html\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_pdf_url\" content=\"https://www.aanda.org/articles/aa/pdf/2016/04/aa27638-15.pdf\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"0004-6361\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_issn\" content=\"1432-0746\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_language\" content=\"en\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"gravitational lensing: strong\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_keyword\" content=\"galaxies: clusters: individual: MACS J0717.5+3745\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_article_type\" content=\"Research Article\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_abstract\" lang=\"en\" content=\"We present a strong-lensing analysis of MACSJ0717.5+3745 (hereafter MACS\u2009J0717), based on the full depth of the &lt;i&gt;Hubble &lt;i/&gt;Frontier Field (HFF) observations, which brings the number of multiply imaged systems to 61, ten of which have been spectroscopically confirmed. The total number of images comprised in these systems rises to 165, compared to 48 images in 16 systems before the HFF observations. Our analysis uses a parametric mass reconstruction technique, as implemented in the Lenstool software, and the subset of the 132 most secure multiple images to constrain a mass distribution composed of four large-scale mass components (spatially aligned with the four main light concentrations) and a multitude of galaxy-scale perturbers. We find a superposition of cored isothermal mass components to provide a good fit to the observational constraints, resulting in a very shallow mass distribution for the smooth (large-scale) component. Given the implications of such a flat mass profile, we investigate whether a model composed of \u201cpeaky\u201d non-cored mass components can also reproduce the observational constraints. We find that such a non-cored mass model reproduces the observational constraints equally well, in the sense that both models give comparable total rms. Although the total (smooth dark matter component plus galaxy-scale perturbers) mass distributions of both models are consistent, as are the integrated two-dimensional mass profiles, we find that the smooth and the galaxy-scale components are very different. We conclude that, even in the HFF era, the generic degeneracy between smooth and galaxy-scale components is not broken, in particular in such a complex galaxy cluster. Consequently, insights into the mass distribution of MACS\u2009J0717 remain limited, emphasizing the need for additional probes beyond strong lensing. Our findings also have implications for estimates of the lensing magnification. We show that the amplification difference between the two models is larger than the error associated with either model, and that this additional systematic uncertainty is approximately the difference in magnification obtained by the different groups of modelers using pre-HFF data. This uncertainty decreases the area of the image plane where we can reliably study the high-redshift Universe by 50 to 70%.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A. class=\"simple-math\">&#177;</span> 15</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">5.5 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#177;</span> 0.3</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">32.5 <span class=\"simple-math\">&#177;</span> 0.35</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">&#8211; </td>\n              </tr>\n              <tr>\n                <td align=\"left\"><span class=\"simple-math\"><i>L</i><sup>&#8727;</sup></span> galaxy</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">&#8211;</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">&#8211;</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">&#8211;</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">&#8211;</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">&#8211;</td>\n                <td align=\"center\">9.2 <span class=\"history\">\n              <p><b>Notes.</b> These parameters correspond to the NFW mass model. Coordinates are given in arcseconds with respect to <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>&#945;</i> = 109.3982<i>,&#948;</i> = 37.745778</span>. The ellipticity <span class=\"simple-math\"><i>e</i></span> is for the mass distribution. Error bars correspond to <span class=\"simple-math\">1<i>&#963;</i></span> confidence level. Concerning the scaling relations, the zero point is set to a magnitude equal to 20.66.</p>\n            </div></div>\n  \n\r\n</div>\r\n\r\n    <div id=\"metrics-tabs\" data-doi=\"10.1051/0004-6361/201527638\" data-edps_ref=\"aa27638-15\">\n<nav class=\"toolbar\">\n\t<button class=\"toolbar-item\" id=\"metrics-siq\">Current usage metrics</button>\n\t<button class=\"toolbar-item\" id=\"info\">About article metrics</button>\n    \n\t\n\t<button class=\"toolbar-item\" id=\"return\">Return to article</button>\n</nav>\n\n<div class=\"panel\" data-for=\"metrics-siq\">\n</div>\n\n<div class=\"panel\" data-for=\"metrics-alm\"></div>\n\n<div class=\"panel\" data-for=\"info\">\n\t\n\n\t<p>Current usage metrics show cumulative count of Article Views (full-text article views including HTML views, PDF and ePub downloads, according to the available data)  and Abstracts Views on Vision4Press platform.</p>\n\n\t<p>Data correspond to usage on the plateform after 2015. The total number of images comprised in these systems rises to 165, compared to 48 images in 16 systems before the HFF observations. Our analysis uses a parametric mass reconstruction technique, as implemented in the Lenstool software, and the subset of the 132 most secure multiple images to constrain a mass distribution composed of four large-scale mass components (spatially aligned with the four main light concentrations) and a multitude of galaxy-scale perturbers. We find a superposition of cored isothermal mass components to provide a good fit to the observational constraints, resulting in a very shallow mass distribution for the smooth (large-scale) component. Given the implications of such a flat mass profile, we investigate whether a model composed of \u201cpeaky\u201d non-cored mass components can also reproduce the observational constraints. We find that such a non-cored mass model reproduces the observational constraints equally well, in the sense that both models give comparable total rms. Although the total (smooth dark matter component plus galaxy-scale perturbers) mass distributions of both models are consistent, as are the integrated two-dimensional mass profiles, we find that the smooth and the galaxy-scale components are very different. We conclude that, even in the HFF era, the generic degeneracy between smooth and galaxy-scale components is not broken, in particular in such a complex galaxy cluster. Consequently, insights into the mass distribution of MACS\u2009J0717 remain limited, emphasizing the need for additional probes beyond strong lensing. Our findings also have implications for estimates of the lensing magnification. We show that the amplification difference between the two models is larger than the error associated with either model, and that this additional systematic uncertainty is approximately the difference in magnification obtained by the different groups of modelers using pre-HFF data. This uncertainty decreases the area of the image plane where we can reliably study the high-redshift Universe by 50 to 70%.\">\n  <meta name=\"citation_reference\" content=\"citation_author=A.
